					- We then ensemble resnet18 and densenet121 using MG-SDWFM and apply it on mammograms. The experimental results on the in-house dataset show the effectiveness of the proposed over other state-of-the-art methods, achieving an AUC of 0.885.
					- In the fusion process, a shared latent embedding $L$ is introduced to represent the most essential features for classification. With the help of the inner product, the similarity between $L$ and each vectorized feature is calculated and the relative importance of different features is then obtained in the form of weights.
					- All individual features are vectorized through linear transformation first. Then their similarities with a learnable latent embedding, which is introduced to denote most task-related features, are calculated using inner product. With larger similarity, there is greater significance that feature. After normalizing the similarity values among features within each group, the corresponding weights are computed.
					- Apparently a feature with a larger similarity means a greater significance, so we obtain corresponding weights by normalizing the similarity values among features within each group.
				- DONE ä¿®æ”¹ä»‹ç»éƒ¨åˆ†çš„æ­£æ–‡
				  :LOGBOOK:
				  CLOCK: [2023-04-05 Wed 16:40:43]--[2023-04-06 Thu 10:23:28] =>  17:42:45
				  :END:
					- Depending on the distribution of MCs, the abnormality can be classified into 7 levels, ranging from BI-RADS (Breast Imaging Reporting and Data Sytem) 0 to BI-RADS 6. The BI-RADS 4 means the MCs are highly suspicious for malignancy and require biopsy for final confirmation of being cancerous (malignant) or noncancerous (benign).
						- The Breast Imaging Reporting and Data Sytem (BI-RADS) has defined 7 levels of abnormality according to the distribution of MCs. BI-RADS 4 warrants special attention as it indicates a highly suspicious malignancy but requires further confirmation through biopsy to determine if it is malignant (cancerous) or benign (noncancerous).
					- In order to reduce the pain of patients caused by excess biopsies, making further diagnosis of BI-RADS 4 cases accurately, i.e. labeling it as benign or malignant, has become gradually important.
						- Therefore, to reduce the pain of patients caused by excess biopsies, making accurate classification of BI-RADS 4 cases has become increasingly significant.
					- there is a large variance of MCs among different patients. However, under true circumstances, there is a large variance of MCs among different patients. Specifically, MCs usually have a radius size that ranges mostly from 0.1 to 1.0 mm, even sometimes $<$ 0.1 mm [11]. This issue makes doctors' years of experience sometimes unreliable and requires doctors to spend more time performing a diagnosis. Therefore, there is a strong demand of achieving diagnostic automation and improving the diagnosis performance.
						- ä¸åŒç—…äººé’¼é¶å›¾åƒä¸Šçš„é’™åŒ–ç‚¹å…·æœ‰å¾ˆå¤§çš„æ–¹å·®
						- In clinical practice, a notable variance of MCs exists among different patients. Typically, MCs have a radius size ranging from 0.1 to 1.0 mm, and occasionally less than 0.1 mm [11]. Consequently,  the diagnostic procedure would take longer and heavily rely on the personal experience of physicians, ultimately affecting the quality of diagnosis. Nowadays the automated diagnosis of BI-RADS 4 cases has been in high demand.
						-
					- In the literature, clustered MCs can be classified by traditional machine learning or traditional deep learning. Traditional machine learning takes a two-steps strategy. The first step is feature extraction, which refers to the use of engineering methods to generate and filter out handcrafted features. For example, Li et al. [13] extracted 837 texture features and 9 shape features from raw images. Fanizzi et al. [16] performed a multi-scale image decomposition based on the Haar wavelet transform and then extracted features on each decomposition. To make features more informative, some work turn to research on the topological structure of the graph formed by MCs. Alam et al. [14] generated a series of multi-scale MC cluster graphs to investigate the scale-specific graph topological changes. Notably, filtering schema is also important in this step. Alam et al. [17] employed a correlation-based feature selection technique and discussed clinical relevance of the selected features. Avsar et al. [18] reduced irrelevant features using principal component analysis (PCA) [19]. The second step is feature classification. Off-the-shelf models of machine learning are used directly here, such as KNN [20], AdaBoost [21], Random Forest [22], and Gaussian Naive Bayes [23]. However, although the first step provides some interpretability, it is time-consuming; in the second step, models usually have poor performance. 
					  Later, deep learning methods, have been successfully applied to many medical image analysis tasks, including image classification [24][25]. Multi-task strategy has gained popularity in its employment. Y. C. Hsieh et al. [26] first used VGG16 and Mask RCNN to find MCs, and then used Inception V3 to identify benignity and malignancy. But this is a multi-stage method. X. Ouyang et al. [27] proposed an end-to-end model combining classification, segmentation and clustering detection. However, these models tend to be overfitting and have poor generalization performance due to huge parameters.
						- In the literature, clustered MCs can be classified by either traditional machine learning or deep learning methods. Traditional machine learning typically involves a two-step strategy. The first step involves feature extraction, which employs engineering methods to generate and filter out handcrafted features. For instance, Li et al. [13] extracted 837 texture features and 9 shape features from raw images, while Fanizzi et al. [16] performed a multi-scale image decomposition by the Haar wavelet transform before extracting features on each decomposition. Some studies also investigate the topological structure of the graph formed by MCs. For instance, Alam et al. [14] generated multi-scale MC cluster graphs to investigate scale-specific graph features. Notably, filtering schema is also important in this step. Alam et al. [17] employed a correlation-based feature selection technique and discussed clinical relevance of the selected features. And Avsar et al. [18] removed irrelevant features using principal component analysis (PCA) [19]. In the second step, off-the-shelf machine learning models like KNN [20], AdaBoost [21], Random Forest [22], and Gaussian Naive Bayes [23] are used for feature classification. However, it is unconvenient to manually select features and set parameters; and the model performance tends to be easily affected by the dataset itself [].
						-
						- In recent years, deep learning methods have been successfully applied to many medical image analysis tasks, including image classification [24][25]. Y. C. Hsieh et al. [26] first applied VGG16 and Mask RCNN to locate MCs, and then utilized Inception V3 for benign-malignant classification. Apparently this is a multi-stage method. X. Ouyang et al. [27] proposed an end-to-end model combining classification, segmentation and clustering detection. Nevertheless, these models tend to be overfitting and have poor generalization performance due to huge parameters of complicated models.
					- Deep ensembling has been widely applied in image classification, approximately 22.5\% of its total applications [28]. However, it has only been applied on breast histopathology images but seldom on mammograms.
					  For example, Z Hameed et al. [33] took simple averaging to ensemble VGG16 and VGG19 for the classification of non-carcinoma and carcinoma breast cancer histopathology images.
					- So in the paper, we decide to explore the use of deep ensemble learning on classification of mammograms MCs. Of all current ensemble strategies, decision fusion matters. It means aggregating the outputs of well trained base learners using certain rules [28]. The rules of ensembling outputs mostly follow naive weighted average which performs either on the direct outputs or on the predicted probabilities [28]. However, it is not data adaptive due to the fixed weights; it also tends to be less optimal [29] because it is sensitive to the performance of the biased learners. To resolve the data-adaption issues, unweighted averaging has been further researched. Bayes Optimal Classifier represented each base learner as a hypothesis and used the sum of likelihood to predict [28]. But the weight vector would be dominated by a single base learner when the sample size is large [28]. Van der Laan et al. [30] proposed super learner which used cross validation to select the optimal weights for combining the predictions of the base learners. Stacked generalization [31] used cross-validation data and least squares under non-negativity constraints [32] to help meta learner learn the weights. Nevertheless, these implementations of data-adaption are dependent on complex mathematical theories or cross-validation tricks.
						- Of available ensemble strategies, decision fusion is one of the most commonly used which aggregates the outputs of well trained base models using certain rules []. The rule mostly followed is naive weighted average that perform either on the direct outputs or on the predicted probabilities. It should be clarified here that each model corresponds to a weight. However, it can be sensitive to biased models, which may be assigned large weights even if they perform poorly on certain data subsets []. To achieve data-adaption, two types of dynamic weights calculation are adopted. The first type is data-driven. For instance, each base model was represented as a hypothesis in Bayes Optimal Classifier and weights were obtained by maximizing the expected logarithmic posterior probability []. Van der Laan et al. []  used cross validation to select the optimal weights for combining the predictions of the base models and proposed super model. The second type is model-driven. Stacked generalization [] used cross-validation data and least squares under non-negativity constraints [] to help meta model learn the weights. Nevertheless, these implementations of data-adaption are dependent on complex mathematical or training tricks.
					- Deep ensembling has been widely applied in image classification, approximately 22.5\% of its total applications [28]. However, it has only been applied on breast histopathology images but seldom on mammograms.
					  For example, Z Hameed et al. [33] took simple averaging to ensemble VGG16 and VGG19 for the classification of non-carcinoma and carcinoma breast cancer histopathology images.
					- So in the paper, we 
					  decide to explore the use of deep ensemble learning on classification of mammograms MCs. Of all current ensemble strategies, decision fusion matters. It means aggregating the outputs of well trained base learners using certain rules [28]. The rules of ensembling outputs mostly follow naive unweighted averaging which performs either on the direct outputs or on the predicted probabilities [28]. However, it is not data adaptive due to the fixed weights; it also tends to be less optimal [29] because it is sensitive to the performance of the biased learners. To resolve the data-adaption issues, unweighted averaging has been further researched. Bayes Optimal Classifier represented each base learner as a hypothesis and used the sum of likelihood to predict [28]. But the weight vector would be dominated by a single base learner when the sample size is large [28]. Van der Laan et al. [30] proposed super learner which used cross validation to select the optimal weights for combining the predictions of the base learners. Stacked generalization [31] used cross-validation data and least squares under non-negativity constraints [32] to help meta learner learn the weights. Nevertheless, these implementations of data-adaption are dependent on complex mathematical theories
					  or cross-validation tricks.
					- The sensitivity comes from the fact that all individual features produced by single model are assigned the same weight. However, inspired from radiomics, these features should have varying degrees of relevance to the classification object. In order to calculate a unique weight for every feature, we invented a multi-group strategy.  To achieve data-adaption in a simple way, we design a similarity-decoding-based method to calculate weights within each group. For brevity, we denote this feture-level data-adaptive strategy for deep models ensembling as multi-group similarity-decoding-based weighted fusion mechanism (MG-SDWFM). When applying MG-SDWFM on classification of mamograms MCs, we choose two models, resnet18 and densenet121, to ensemble.
						- To mitigate sensitivity, we developed a multi-group strategy to assign unique weights to each individual feature produced by a single model. This strategy was inspired by radiomics [], where features should have varying relevance to classification task. To achieve simple data-adaption, we designed a similarity-decoding-based approach to calculate weights within each group. To be concise, we refer to the proposed procedure for ensembling deep models as the multi-group similarity-decoding-based method (MG-SDM). MG-SD was then applied to ensemble resnet18 and densenet121 on the task of MCs classification.
						-

					- We proposed a multi-group similarity-decoding-based method (MG-SDM) for deep model ensembling.  And MG-SDM was successfully utilized to ensemble resnet18 and densenet121. On clinical dataset, the proposed outperforms resnet18 or densenet121 alone and the concatenation fusion strategy, demonstrating the effectiveness of our scheme.
					- On the classification of MCs scored at BI-RADS 4, the proposed beat machine learning and traditional deep models in terms of both qualitative and quantitative performance. Through Grad-CAM visualizations, we demonstrate that our method not only identifies calcifications, but also accurately locates them with high precision.
					- With the capability of fusing multiple feature vectors of equal length, MG-SDM could establish the concept of weighted pooling by replacing the global average pooling operation. By applying this concept separately to resnet18 and densenet121, we observed improved performance. This further demonstrates the rationale behind the utilization of MG-SDM.
					- We add an auxiliary output for resnet18 and densenet121 separately and design a multi-output weighted loss to provide supervision. This alleviates the training difficulties caused by parameter proliferation and allows for single-pass training without additional pre-training.

						- å¯ä»¥å…ˆæè¿°ä¸ºå•¥éœ€è¦æ”¹åŠ¨ã€æ€ä¹ˆæ”¹åŠ¨ã€ç„¶åæ”¹åŠ¨åçš„ç”¨æ³•
						- ç„¶åå…³äºæ¨¡å‹çš„è®­ç»ƒå†å•ç‹¬å†™ä¸€æ®µå§ï¼Œæ²¡æœ‰å¿…è¦å†è¿™é‡Œæ’å…¥ï¼Œæ˜¾å¾—å¾ˆæ··ä¹±
						- ç°åœ¨çš„éš¾ç‚¹æ˜¯éœ€è¦æŠŠè¿™ä¸ªpipelineä¸­æˆ‘ä»¬æ¨¡å‹çš„ä¼˜åŠ¿å’Œå…¶ä»–æ¨¡å‹çš„åŒºåˆ«çªå‡ºï¼ŒåŒæ—¶éœ€è¦æŠŠè¿™ä¸ªè¿‡ç¨‹æè¿°å¾—æ›´åŠ è¯¦ç»†ä¸€äº›ï¼šæˆ‘è§‰å¾—å¾—æŠŠè¿™ä¸ªåŠ æƒçš„è¿‡ç¨‹ç»™å†™ä¸€ä¸‹ï¼Œè®©åˆ«äººæ›´å¥½ç†è§£ï¼›
						- On the classification task of  mammographic images, resnet18 and densenet121 has both been adopted to extract morphological, textural and edgel features of MCs [][].  Besides, they can theoretically capture complementary features as resnet18 can well extract shallow features and reuse them while densenet121 can extract deep features and discover new ones []. Therefore, they are selected as two basic models to be ensembled.
							- For the classification of mammographic images, resnet18 and densenet121 have been once used to extract morphological, textural, and edge features of microcalcifications (MCs) []. Moreover, resnet18 can efficiently extract shallow features and reuse them, while densenet121 can extract deep features and discover new ones []. Therefore, these two models are chosen as basic models to be ensembled, as they can theoretically capture complementary features.
						- Two modifications are made on the structure. Firstly,  we adjust backbones' structures from a conventional single Fc (fully connected layer) into two consecutive Fcs  (see $fc_1$ and $fc_2$ in Fig. 4). And two $c_1$-lengthy feature vectors $m$ and $n$ are obtained right after corresponding $fc_1$. The reason is that the number of output neurons of the Fc (i.e. the number of categories N) is insufficient for effective fusion. To provide supervision for feature extraction, we also allow addition outputs of classification from $fc_2$ and adopt the multi-output weighted loss function to train the model. Secondly,  $m$ and $n$ are fused into  vector $f$ with the same length of $c_1$ in the model ensembling block. The block functions through our proposed MG-SDM.
							- To ensemble resnet18 and desnet121,  their classification heads were adjusted from one single fully connected layer (FC) into two consecutive FCs (see $fc_1$ and $fc_2$ in Fig. 4 (b)). We made this modification because the dimensionality of the original FC (i.e. the number of categories N) was insufficient for effective information fusion. The first FC layer is used to generate dense feature vectors. In our case, two $c_1$-lengthy feature vectors, $m$ and $n$, are obtained from the first FC layer of the two models, respectively. Then in the model ensembling block, $m$ and $n$ are weightedly fused into a more informative vector $f$ using the proposed multi-group similarity-decoding-based method (MG-SDM). The second FC layer still outputs the classification results, which provides certain supervision for the feature extraction of a single branch. With the existence of additional outputs, we designed a multi-output weighted loss function to train the whole model in an end-to-end manner.

				- We use accuracy, sensitivity and specificity as metrics for classification. The accuracy describes the proportion of correctly predicted samples to the total number of samples. Sensitivity describes the proportion of actual positive samples that are correctly predicted as positive, while specificity describes the proportion of actual negative samples that are correctly predicted as negative. The specific formulas for these metrics is as follows, where TP, TN, FP, and FN respectively represent the number of true positives, true negatives, false positives, and false negatives:
				- è¿‘å¹´æ¥ï¼Œæ·±åº¦å­¦ä¹ åœ¨å„ç§ä¸åŒç±»å‹çš„ä»»åŠ¡ä¸Šéƒ½å–å¾—äº†çªç ´ï¼Œæ¯”å¦‚[]æå‡ºäº†ä¸€ç§åŸºäºçŸ¥è¯†å›¾çš„æ¨¡å‹Rec-RNç”¨äºç‰©å“æ¨èï¼Œ[]æå‡ºäº†ä¸€ç§è‡ªåŠ¨åŒ–çš„è§†é¢‘åˆ†ææ¡†æ¶æ¥è¯†åˆ«æ›å…‰åŒºåŸŸã€‚å½“ç„¶ï¼Œ
					- In recent years, deep learning has achieved significant breakthroughs in various types of tasks. For example, [19] proposed a knowledge graph-based model Rec-RN for item recommendation, while [20] presented an automated video analysis framework to identify the exposure region. 					- In recent years, deep learning has made significant breakthroughs across various types of tasks. Furthermore, it is worth noting that deep learning techniques have also found successful applications in medical image analysis tasks, such as image classification [][].
